<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spacewalks">Spacewalks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-132&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Spacewalks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Three spacewalks were conducted to replace six aging batteries and to stage spare components outside the station, including a secondary K<sub>u</sub> band antenna and spares for the Canadian <a href="/wiki/Dextre" title="Dextre">Dextre</a> robotic arm extension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAfacts_Remaining_Space_Shuttle_Missions_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASAfacts_Remaining_Space_Shuttle_Missions-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th width="10%">EVA<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summary_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-summary-102">[102]</a></sup></th>
<th width="20%">Spacewalkers</th>
<th width="16%">Start (<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>)</th>
<th width="16%">End (UTC)</th>
<th width="12%">Duration</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2">EVA 1</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Garrett_Reisman" title="Garrett Reisman">Garrett Reisman</a><br/>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_G._Bowen" title="Stephen G. Bowen">Steve Bowen</a></td>
<td>17 May 2010<br/>
11:54</td>
<td>17 May 2010<br/>
19:19</td>
<td>7 hours 25 minutes</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="4">Reisman and Bowen installed a spare space-to-ground <a href="/wiki/Ku_band" title="Ku band">K<sub>u</sub> band</a> antenna on the station's truss, or backbone. They then installed a new tool platform on Dextre. The spacewalkers also broke the torque on bolts holding batteries in place on the truss, in preparation for their removal and replacement on the second and third spacewalks.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2">EVA 2</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_G._Bowen" title="Stephen G. Bowen">Steve Bowen</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Michael_T._Good" title="Michael T. Good">Michael Good</a></td>
<td>19 May 2010<br/>
10:38</td>
<td>19 May 2010<br/>
17:47</td>
<td>7 hours 9 minutes</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="4">Bowen and Good removed and replaced four of the six batteries on the port truss to store electricity from the solar arrays on that truss. The used batteries were installed on the cargo carrier for return to Earth on <i>Atlantis</i>. They also fixed a snagged cable on the Orbiter Boom Sensor System. The final task was to re-torque the bolts on the SGANT and then remove the launch locks and tether that were helping hold it in place.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2">EVA 3</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Michael_T._Good" title="Michael T. Good">Michael Good</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Garrett_Reisman" title="Garrett Reisman">Garrett Reisman</a></td>
<td>21 May 2010<br/>
10:27</td>
<td>21 May 2010<br/>
17:13</td>
<td>6 hours 46 minutes</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="4">Good and Reisman first connected a liquid ammonia jumper hose. They then installed the final two new batteries on the truss and put the old batteries on the carrier. Next, they retrieved a grapple fixture from Atlantis' payload bay and brought it inside the station to be modified for future installation on the <a href="/wiki/Zarya" title="Zarya">Zarya</a> module. The pair also stowed some tools in an external toolbox outside the airlock for future spacewalks.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_insignia">Mission insignia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-132&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Mission insignia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The STS-132 <a href="/wiki/Mission_patch" title="Mission patch">mission patch</a> was designed by NASA artist Sean Collins, working with astronaut Garrett Reisman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summary_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-summary-102">[102]</a></sup> The patch shows <i>Atlantis</i> flying towards a sunset landing, with the names of the STS-132 astronauts around the border.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="STS-132_mission_decal">STS-132 mission decal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-132&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: STS-132 mission decal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During the standard post-flight inspection of Atlantis, a United Space Alliance inspector found a STS-132 mission decal accompanied by an inscription, "<i>The first last flight of Atlantis left Earth on 14 May 2010 from Pad 39A</i>" together with the crew's signatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The worker had found it tucked away on the upper side of Locker A-16 while scanning the area with a mirror. Moreover, he said the note must have been written in orbit, since otherwise the author would have had to stand on their head to write it.</p>
<p>At the time the note was written, STS-132 was indeed the last planned mission of <i>Atlantis</i>. However, one further mission was ultimately approved for the shuttle: <a href="/wiki/STS-135" title="STS-135">STS-135</a>, which will be the last flight of both <i>Atlantis</i> and the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">Space Shuttle program</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wake-up_calls">Wake-up calls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-132&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Wake-up calls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>NASA began a tradition of playing music to astronauts during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gemini_program" title="Gemini program">Gemini program</a>, and first used music to wake up a flight crew during <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">Apollo 15</a>. Each track is specially chosen, often by the astronauts' families, and usually has a special meaning to an individual member of the crew, or is applicable to their daily activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronology_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-chronology-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wakeup_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-wakeup-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
